Kubernetes codebase, controllers register with the manager using a descriptor-based registration pattern. Here's how the registration flow works:\\n\\n1. CONTROLLER INTERFACE DEFINITION (staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go, line 26):\\nThe base controller.Interface defines a simple Name() string method that all controllers must implement. Controllers may optionally implement controller.Debuggable (line 36) for debug endpoints or controller.HealthCheckable (line 50) for health checks.\\n\\n2. CONTROLLER DESCRIPTOR (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go, line 421):\\nEach controller is wrapped in a ControllerDescriptor that holds:\\n- name: The canonical name of the controller\\n- initFunc: An InitFunc callback that creates and starts the controller\\n- requiredFeatureGates: Feature gates that must be enabled\\n- aliases: Backwards-compatible name aliases\\n- isDisabledByDefault: Whether the controller is disabled by default\\n\\n3. INITFUNC TYPE (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go, line 419):\\nInitFunc is defined as: func(ctx context.Context, controllerContext ControllerContext, controllerName string) (controller.Interface, bool, error)\\nIt takes a ControllerContext which provides access to informers, clients, and configuration (defined in staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/app/controllercontext.go).\\n\\n4. CONTROLLER REGISTRATION (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go, line 495-593):\\nIn NewControllerDescriptors(), controllers are registered by calling register() for each controller descriptor. For example:\\n- newEndpointsControllerDescriptor() (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/core.go, line 423)\\n- newReplicationControllerDescriptor() (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/core.go, line 443)\\nEach returns a ControllerDescriptor with an associated startXxxController InitFunc.\\n\\n5. STARTUP AND REGISTRATION (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go, line 662-761):\\nWhen the manager runs:\\n- StartControllers() iterates through controller descriptors\\n- For each controller, StartController() is called\\n- StartController() calls the controller's InitFunc (line 737)\\n- The InitFunc creates and starts the actual controller (e.g., via go controller.Run())\\n- The controller can implement controller.Debuggable and controller.HealthCheckable interfaces to register debug handlers and health checks\\n\\n6. CONCRETE EXAMPLE - ENDPOINTS CONTROLLER (pkg/controller/endpoint/endpoints_controller.go):\\n- NewEndpointController() creates a Controller struct (line 73)\\n- It registers event handlers on informers (lines 89-108)\\n- The Run() method (line 171) implements the reconciliation loop:\\n  - Waits for caches to sync\\n  - Starts worker goroutines\\n  - Workers process items from the workqueue\\n  - Handles pod/service changes and syncs endpoints\\n\\nKey difference from sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime: Kubernetes uses a lightweight manager in staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager that doesn't use the Reconciler interface or SetupWithManager pattern. Instead, it uses InitFunc callbacks and direct controller instantiation. Kubernetes codebase, controllers register with the manager using a descriptor-based registration pattern. Here's how the registration flow works:\\n\\n1. CONTROLLER INTERFACE DEFINITION (staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go, line 26):\\nThe base controller.Interface defines a simple Name() string method that all controllers must implement. Controllers may optionally implement controller.Debuggable (line 36) for debug endpoints or controller.HealthCheckable (line 50) for health checks.\\n\\n2. CONTROLLER DESCRIPTOR (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go, line 421):\\nEach controller is wrapped in a ControllerDescriptor that holds:\\n- name: The canonical name of the controller\\n- initFunc: An InitFunc callback that creates and starts the controller\\n- requiredFeatureGates: Feature gates that must be enabled\\n- aliases: Backwards-compatible name aliases\\n- isDisabledByDefault: Whether the controller is disabled by default\\n\\n3. INITFUNC TYPE (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go, line 419):\\nInitFunc is defined as: func(ctx context.Context, controllerContext ControllerContext, controllerName string) (controller.Interface, bool, error)\\nIt takes a ControllerContext which provides access to informers, clients, and configuration (defined in staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/app/controllercontext.go).\\n\\n4. CONTROLLER REGISTRATION (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go, line 495-593):\\nIn NewControllerDescriptors(), controllers are registered by calling register() for each controller descriptor. For example:\\n- newEndpointsControllerDescriptor() (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/core.go, line 423)\\n- newReplicationControllerDescriptor() (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/core.go, line 443)\\nEach returns a ControllerDescriptor with an associated startXxxController InitFunc.\\n\\n5. STARTUP AND REGISTRATION (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go, line 662-761):\\nWhen the manager runs:\\n- StartControllers() iterates through controller descriptors\\n- For each controller, StartController() is called\\n- StartController() calls the controller's InitFunc (line 737)\\n- The InitFunc creates and starts the actual controller (e.g., via go controller.Run())\\n- The controller can implement controller.Debuggable and controller.HealthCheckable interfaces to register debug handlers and health checks\\n\\n6. CONCRETE EXAMPLE - ENDPOINTS CONTROLLER (pkg/controller/endpoint/endpoints_controller.go):\\n- NewEndpointController() creates a Controller struct (line 73)\\n- It registers event handlers on informers (lines 89-108)\\n- The Run() method (line 171) implements the reconciliation loop:\\n  - Waits for caches to sync\\n  - Starts worker goroutines\\n  - Workers process items from the workqueue\\n  - Handles pod/service changes and syncs endpoints\\n\\nKey difference from sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime: Kubernetes uses a lightweight manager in staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager that doesn't use the Reconciler interface or SetupWithManager pattern. Instead, it uses InitFunc callbacks and direct controller instantiation. Controllers are responsible for their own event handling and work loop implementation using client-go informers and workqueues.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
